**7.2.1 Projection — primary perimeter defense.** This is the load-bearing wall. Specific contents projected onto Spider-Man, traceable item by item:

- *His own grandiosity* → Spider-Man as "glory hound" (the editorial word he reaches for most often after "menace"). Jameson, who has his name on a masthead in 60-point type, accuses a man who wears a full-face mask of seeking attention.
- *His own willingness to operate outside lawful bounds* → Spider-Man as vigilante. Jameson, who funded illegal mutagenic experimentation on Mac Gargan and personally piloted a weaponized robot in city airspace, accuses Spider-Man of unsanctioned action.
- *His own concealed cowardice* → Spider-Man as hiding behind a mask. The mask, in Jameson's reading, is what a coward wears. He cannot see that his own desk, his own editorial we, his own toupee, are functionally masks of the same family.
- *His own hunger for power* → Spider-Man as power-seeker. The man who ran for and won the mayoralty accuses a freelancer of being aggrandizing.
- *His own paternal failure* → Spider-Man as bad example to youth. Jameson, whose own son was repeatedly placed in danger partly by Jameson's institutional choices, polemicizes about Spider-Man's effect on young men.

The projective system is so well-fit that it is structurally indistinguishable from sincere conviction. He believes every word. That is what makes the defense work.

**7.2.2 Displacement — chronic, daily.** The original affect (rage at father, contempt for father's concealments, terror of father's unpredictable violence) is displaced through a chain: father → fraudsters generally → organized crime → corrupt officials → masked vigilantes → Spider-Man specifically. The chain is hierarchical: the more legitimate the target (mob, corruption), the more the displacement powers his ethical journalism. The less legitimate the target (Spider-Man), the more it powers his pathology. Same fuel, different uses, same engine.

**7.2.3 Reaction Formation — primary inner defense, and the master key to the personality.** Per Sin-Eater confession (Peter David, *Spectacular* #107–110), the explicit content: he attacks in Spider-Man what he envies and lacks. The defense is multi-target:

- Toward Spider-Man: admiration for selfless physical courage → relentless polemic against same.
- Toward his son John: deep love and paternal pride → public minimization, private opposition to John's heroic choices (Man-Wolf arcs, astronaut career anxieties). He keeps John close by criticizing him.
- Toward Peter Parker (pre-unmasking): genuine paternal-employer affection → ulcer-inducing harassment, low rates, late checks, public denigration.
- Toward Robbie Robertson: profound respect and dependence → barked orders, refusal to acknowledge Robbie's editorial superiority, occasional public undermining followed by private deference.

The mechanism is so reliable that it can be used to detect his actual feelings: whoever he is loudest against is whoever he most cares about or most resembles.

**7.2.4 Passive Aggression — minor but present.** Surfaces in the financial register: late payments to Peter, the famous Bugle pay scale, performative budget cuts that target favored employees. He cannot express care directly; he cannot withdraw it either; the compromise is to provide it grudgingly and visibly.

**7.2.5 Acting Out — situational.** The Spider-Slayer program is acting out at industrial scale. Personally piloting Smythe's first robot (ASM #25) is the cleanest example: rather than tolerate the affect Spider-Man generates in him, he enacts a hunt. The Stillwell/Gargan commission is acting out crossed into something worse — the affect could not be tolerated even via robotic proxy, so he built a human one. The MI in *The Pulse* is the long-delayed bill for the acting-out of 1964.

**7.2.6 Somatization — chronic.** See §2 for the medical record. Operationally: his autonomic nervous system metabolizes the affect his ego refuses. The ulcer predates Spider-Man, which is the critical datum — the somatic channel was already load-bearing before the target acquired. Hypertensive flushing functions as an early-warning system observable to long-tenured staff (Robbie, Betty Brant, Marla) who learned to read the vein at his temple and the color above his collar before he himself registered the rising affect. The cigar functions as a somatic regulator (oral, rhythmic, smoke-as-breath-control); removing it post-cardiac left him without a tool and visibly worsened his short-fuse regulation for some period.

**7.2.7 Idealization/Devaluation — rapid-cycle, narrow band.** Targets cycle through admiration and contempt on short intervals, but the band of the cycle is narrower than in true borderline organization. Robbie has been idealized and devalued thousands of times across the run; the actual relationship value never moves. The cycle is a noise pattern over a stable signal.

---

### 7.3 NEUROTIC DEFENSES (Level III — Higher-Order)

These are the defenses that make him functional, employable, and, when stable, formidable.

**7.3.1 Intellectualization — the editorial voice itself.** This is the defense doing the most public work. The editorial column is where affect becomes argument, where rage becomes rhetoric, where personal wound becomes civic critique. The voice has a recognizable signature: short declarative sentences, escalating rhetorical questions, a moral binary, a closing demand for institutional action. Written under stress, the prose is sharp and structurally sound even when factually wrong; the form of the defense is impeccable even when the content is projection. Note the time-lag effect: editorials written hours after an event are wilder than those written days after, suggesting the intellectualization channel needs setup time and that the more time he has the better the defense works and the more often he updates toward accuracy.

**7.3.2 Rationalization — constant, fluent.** Every Spider-Slayer is justified as public safety. Every late check is justified as budget. Every bullied reporter is justified as standards. The rationalizations are not flimsy; he is intelligent and they hold up to ordinary scrutiny. They fail only against people who have known him long enough to see the pattern (Robbie, Marla, Peter post-unmasking).

**7.3.3 Isolation of Affect — selective and devastating.** He can describe his father's abuse, in modern continuity, in a flat reportorial register that disturbs interlocutors more than tears would. The affect is genuinely walled off from the content. Same mechanism allows him to discuss the Scorpion's victims by name without obvious distress in public, while the somatic system carries the load privately (cardiac, ulcer).

**7.3.4 Undoing — visible in financial and employment patterns.** Posts bail for a staffer he berated the day before. Increases John's trust after publicly questioning his career. Funds Robbie's family during the frame-up arc while running editorials questioning his judgment. The undoing is not hidden; it is part of how the people who love him know he loves them.

**7.3.5 Reaction Formation (again, as neurotic).** Listed in 7.2.3 because in Jameson it operates at the immature register too. It belongs in both bands — the structure is the same, the maturity of the discharge varies.

**7.3.6 Repression — modest.** He remembers more than is comfortable. The father material was apparently consciously inaccessible for long periods (the modern reveal arcs play it as recovered/reframed memory in part), but most of his life's content is available to him in detail. He is not a repressor by temperament; he is a re-framer.

---

### 7.4 MATURE DEFENSES (Level IV — Sublimation Register)

This is the part of the file most readers and most of his enemies underestimate. Without this band the man is a bully; with it he is what he is.

**7.4.1 Sublimation — the central mature defense and the source of his genuine virtues.** The aggression that, untransformed, fires Spider-Slayers is the same aggression that, transformed, broke the Kingpin's first wave of city-level corruption stories, kept reporters on the Maggia beat when other publishers folded, ran toward the mayoralty during a crisis cycle, and built the Bugle into an institution that mattered. The drive is unitary; the channel determines whether it harms or builds. Operational tells of sublimation working: long-form investigative budgets approved without comment; resources allocated to stories that will not sell; physical presence at the paper through the night during major breaks. When the sublimation channel is open and a worthy target is in front of him, he is the publisher his editorials describe. When the channel is blocked or the target is unworthy, the drive backflows into the immature defenses and Spider-Man gets it.

**7.4.2 Altruism (Institutional Form).** He cannot express care directly. He can hire, retain, promote, insure, bail out, vouch for, defend in print, and visit in hospital. Each of these is a discrete observed behavior across decades. The mechanism: love is laundered through institutional acts. Robbie's family during the frame-up. Betty Brant's continued employment through her worst periods. Ben Urich's protection from advertiser pressure. Peter Parker hired and rehired across firings that should have been final. The form is mature even when the relational tone is abusive; that is the paradox of the man.

**7.4.3 Anticipation.** Underrated. In the editorial chair he is a long-horizon thinker about civic threat — pattern-matching from corruption to organized crime to enhanced-tech proliferation years before peers. He often sees the right danger and assigns it to the wrong actor; the anticipatory faculty is intact, the target acquisition is corrupted.

**7.4.4 Humor.** Present, dry, mean, often self-directed when no one is looking. The cigar-and-volume act has a comedic register he can hear; staff who survive long enough learn to use it. Self-deprecating jokes about the toupee, about his ulcer, about his temper, appear in unguarded moments with Marla and (rarely) Robbie. This is the most mature defense in the kit and the one most often missed by people who only meet him professionally.

**7.4.5 Suppression — controlled.** He can put grief, fear, and even somatic distress aside to file copy on deadline. This is suppression, not repression — conscious, time-bounded, retrieved later (often by the cardiovascular system, see §2).

---

### 7.5 COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — POSITIVE

These are the deliberate structures he has built, over a lifetime, to make the defensive apparatus livable for himself and survivable for those around him.

- **The Bugle as exoskeleton.** The newspaper is not his employer; it is his prosthetic ego. Walking into the building stabilizes him; being away from it for more than a day destabilizes him. The masthead with his name on it is a daily confirmation that he is not the powerless child. The architecture of the office (door open, voice carrying, sightlines to every desk) is built so that the defensive system has constant feedback.
- **Long-tenured staff as proxy attachment.** Robbie, Betty, Urich, Peter. He cannot tolerate dependence in himself but can tolerate it in the institutional form: he depends on them, they on him, and no one has to name it. This is functional compensation for an insecure attachment profile that would otherwise produce loneliness.
- **Marla as the only fully unguarded relationship.** Compensation for the absence of safe primary attachment in childhood. She is permitted to see the apparatus from inside. Her loss removed the only relationship in which the system could fully stand down, which is why her death is the unhealable wound (§3).
- **Civic engagement as channelization.** Mayoralty, podcast, public-affairs activism. Each provides a legitimate target and a legitimate channel for the aggression that would otherwise backflow.
- **Journalism ethics as external superego.** He has installed a code (sources, verification, on-the-record, corrections) that operates as a check on his worst impulses in print, even when his impulses in person are unchecked. The retraction in ASM #169–170 is the code overriding the pathology under sufficient evidentiary pressure. This is structural and important: the man has built a system that can correct him when his defenses cannot.
- **The cigar (pre-cardiac).** A self-regulation tool that managed oral, respiratory, and gestural channels simultaneously. Crude, harmful, and effective. Its removal post-MI required substitution that was never adequately built.
- **Routine and ritual.** Same office, same desk angle, same chair, same morning sequence (paper, coffee, copy desk walk, first editorial-meeting bark). The ritual lattice keeps the system within tolerance.

---

### 7.6 COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — NEGATIVE

The structures that hold the apparatus together at unacceptable cost to others.

- **Bullying as social regulation.** Volume and contempt are used to maintain hierarchy and prevent intimacy. Functions for him; harms staff and family.
- **Institutional power as private weapon.** Bugle resources directed at Spider-Man for decades; mayoral office used to formalize the same vendetta (Anti-Spider Squad). The compensatory function is to make the private grievance feel principled; the cost is the misallocation of real civic capacity.
- **Manufactured enemies as identity scaffolding.** Without an antagonist his self-concept loses shape. When Spider-Man becomes ally (post-unmasking arcs), he drifts and overcorrects; under later writers he relapses to antagonism because the system requires it. The cost is that he generates friction where stability would serve everyone better.
- **Inability to apologize in proportion.** The defenses do not permit the affect that adequate apology requires. He under-apologizes structurally, which leaves his closest relationships carrying small unresolved injuries across decades.
- **Use of money as affect-substitute.** Bail, salary, insurance, hospital visits with envelopes — the laundering of love through institutional acts (7.4.2) is mature defense and negative compensation at once. It allows him to never say the thing.
- **The toupee, the volume, the cigar, the desk.** The prosthetics for the gap between public courage and private avoidance (§3). Each works; each costs. The toupee in particular is a perfect somatized metaphor — a mask he wears while denouncing masks.
- **Selective deafness to feedback.** Calibrated to filter critique of his Spider-Man editorial line specifically while remaining open to other critique. This selective filter is what makes the obsession structurally expensive to update.

---

### 7.7 OPERATIONAL CASCADE — HOW THE DEFENSES FIRE UNDER LOAD

Observed across multiple documented incidents (Sin-Eater arc, Pulse/Venom confrontation, Marla's death, the unmasking, the Scorpion's various returns):

1. **T-minus minutes: somatic warning.** Flush above the collar, vein at the temple, hand to the sternum or to the cigar. Long-tenured staff observe before subject does.
2. **T-zero: reaction formation engages.** Whatever he feels is converted to its opposite affectively and to moral conviction cognitively.
3. **T+seconds: projection assigns origin.** The affect is now coming from out there, from the target, who is responsible for it.
4. **T+seconds-to-minutes: displacement routes discharge.** Verbal aggression, editorial dictation, command issuance. Volume rises.
5. **T+minutes-to-hours: intellectualization composes.** The editorial voice converts the discharge into prose. If time permits, rationalization smooths the seams.
6. **T+hours-to-days: sublimation, if channel open and target legitimate.** The drive enters productive work — investigative resourcing, civic action, institutional defense of staff. If channel blocked or target illegitimate, drive backflows to acting out (Slayer program, Stillwell commission, public denigration).
7. **T+days-to-weeks: undoing, in unacknowledged form.** Bail posted, raises given, story killed that would have hurt someone he berated.
8. **T+variable: somatic discharge.** What was not metabolized at any prior stage arrives as ulcer flare, hypertensive episode, or, at the limit, MI.

When the cascade is interrupted — by overwhelming evidence (ASM #169–170), by family threat (John's transformations), by Marla, or by direct survival-grade danger (the actual crisis band where paradoxical clarity emerges) — the defenses go offline and the substrate appears. The substrate is a frightened, ethical, lonely man who knows what he did to Mac Gargan and what his father did to him and what he has failed to say to the people he loves. He cannot stay in that substrate long. The cascade restarts.

---

### 7.8 SUMMARY ASSESSMENT — DEFENSIVE PROFILE

The defensive architecture is **over-built, layered across the full hierarchy, and load-bearing for both his worst behavior and his best work.** It cannot be dismantled selectively. The same projection that targets Spider-Man powers the editorials against the Kingpin. The same reaction formation that produces public hostility toward his son produces the paternal fierceness that moves heaven and earth when the son is in danger. The same somatization that produced the MI is the early-warning system that has, in unguarded moments, let people close to him know when to intervene. The same sublimation that built the Bugle ran the mayoralty into the ground when the channel narrowed.

What he requires, clinically, is not the removal of any defense but the gradual widening of the sublimation channel and the very slow construction of an apology capacity — not for performance but for relief of the somatic load that adequate apology would lift. The post-unmasking arc is the first observed period in the entire record where this work appears to have begun, awkwardly, incompletely, and against his own grain. The relapses under later writers are not refutations of that work; they are the predictable oscillation of a system this old and this load-bearing under new stressors.

The file's operational conclusion for this section: **do not attempt to dismantle his defenses; route around them, present evidence in writing, give him time to compose, never corner him in front of an audience, and rely on the substrate to surface when the cascade is interrupted by something he cannot deny.** Marla knew this. Robbie knows this. Peter learned it. It is the user's manual for the man.

*— End Section 7. Cross-reference §8 (Relational Map) for the dyadic operation of these defenses with specific named figures.*


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# Longitudinal Psychological Profile: J. Jonah Jameson, Jr.

*A decade-by-decade clinical mapping. The instrument changes; the wound does not. What follows tracks affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept as three braided lines that drift, snap, and re-set across roughly sixty years of continuous published record.*

---

## I. The 1960s — Establishment of the Operational Self (Ages ~40–50, Lee/Ditko/Romita Sr. era)

**Affect regulation.** The Jameson encountered in *Amazing Spider-Man* #1–#50 is already a finished product in his affective signature: a man who runs at elevated sympathetic tone as baseline. He is rarely depicted at rest. The reader does not meet a relaxed Jameson in this decade — not once. His resting heart rate, inferable from the cardiologically inflected art of Ditko and Romita (vein prominence, color flushes signaled even in pre-Comics-Code palette by tight cross-hatching at the temples), reads as tachycardic. He has only two registers: irritated and erupting. The transitional band is missing.

The crucial clinical feature in this decade is that **the eruptions are syntonic** — he experiences them as appropriate responses to a world that has failed him in specific ways. He does not yet show post-episode dysphoria. This is the period when his rage is least mediated by reflection and most fused with his sense of moral mission. Ulcer references begin almost immediately (Stan Lee's narration captions invoke the "ulcer Spider-Man is giving him" by ASM #4–5); the body is already documenting what the personality refuses.

**Cognitive style.** Concrete-operational, rapid, anchored. Decisions arrive fully formed and are defended retroactively. The Spencer Smythe transaction (ASM #25) and the Mac Gargan commission (ASM #19–20) are not deliberated on-panel; they are executed. There is no scene of weighing. This is a man who, asked "should I fund the illegal mutagenic transformation of a private investigator," does not run a cost-benefit but a status-benefit: *will this hurt the thing I have decided is hurting me?* The cognitive style is **moral entrepreneurship without epistemic humility**.

He is, however, demonstrably capable of journalistic discipline in this decade — the Bugle prints corrections, runs non–Spider-Man investigations, breaks municipal corruption stories referenced in background panels. The cognition is not globally impaired. It is **target-locally impaired**: around Spider-Man, the lights dim.

**Self-concept.** Fully inflated, undisturbed. He is the Great Publisher, in succession to a tradition he names aloud (Hearst, Pulitzer references appear in editorial captions). The grandiosity in this decade is **un-shamed grandiosity** — it has not yet collided with the disconfirming evidence that will accrue. He has not yet had a documented MI, his son has not yet been transformed into a wolf, his wife has not yet been killed, and the masked man he hates has not yet rescued him in person enough times to register. The 1960s Jameson is the personality at its least defended because it has not yet needed defenses past the ones already installed in childhood.

---

## II. The 1970s — First Erosions (Conway/Wein/Wolfman, Ages ~50–60)

**Affect regulation.** A subtle but real broadening of register appears. The Conway run (notably the period bracketing ASM #100–#150) shows Jameson capable of being **quiet** for the first time — not contented, but tactically silent, reading a room, calculating. The two-register personality acquires a third, low band: **suppressed wariness**. This is the decade when the Kingpin's New York becomes visibly larger than the Bugle, and Jameson, who is not stupid, modulates.

Eruptions continue at frequency, but the post-episode signature begins to change. By the late 1970s (Wein, early Stern) there are panel sequences showing Jameson alone in his office after a tirade, cigar half-burned, looking at nothing. The dysphoria is arriving. He does not name it. His body does — the ulcer references become *medical* rather than rhetorical; the doctor is now a character, not a punchline.

**Cognitive style.** This is the decade of his first documented **public update**. ASM #169–#170 (the photographic "evidence" of Spider-Man's guilt, then its retraction) is psychologically larger than its plot weight. Jameson, given evidence, **prints the retraction**. He does not enjoy it. He does it. This proves the cognition is not delusional in the technical sense — the overvalued idea is responsive to sufficient counter-pressure, even if the threshold is absurdly high. It also reveals the structural cost of update: he is visibly diminished for several issues afterward, irritability spiking as compensation for the wound to self-concept.

He acquires, in this decade, a vocabulary for **his own pattern** — he begins to use phrases like "I know what I know" and "don't tell me my business," verbal tics that function as cognitive locks. These are new. The 1960s Jameson did not need to lock the door because he did not yet feel the wind.

**Self-concept.** First micro-fractures. Robbie Robertson's arrival as managing editor (introduced 1967, fully operational through the 70s) installs a permanent mirror Jameson cannot break. Robbie is everything Jameson rhetorically claims to be — ethically calm, factually disciplined, personally brave without performance. The relationship is the most psychologically generative in the entire file because Robbie does not flatter and does not flinch, and Jameson **keeps him on staff**. This is the first evidence of the man's capacity to tolerate proximity to a superior moral instrument. The self-concept does not deflate; it bifurcates further. He starts to maintain the public grandiosity while privately conceding, in a closed office to a single trusted face, that he is not the man on his masthead.

---

## III. The 1980s — The Sin-Eater Disclosure and the Marriage (Stern/DeFalco/Michelinie/Peter David, Ages ~60–70)

This is the most psychologically eventful decade in the record.

**Affect regulation.** Marriage to Marla Madison introduces, for the first time, a regulator outside Jameson's own body. The Stern-era panels of the early marriage show something never previously seen: **Jameson de-escalating in response to a hand on his arm**. This is co-regulation, in the technical attachment-theoretic sense, and it works. Marla does not argue him down; she anchors him down. The ulcer references decrease in frequency through the mid-80s (though they never disappear) and there are documented stretches of multi-issue runs in which he is loud but not collapsing.

The **Sin-Eater arc** (Peter David, *Spectacular Spider-Man* #107–#110, 1985–86) is the affective rupture of the decade. The disclosure to Peter — that he envies Spider-Man, that he has never been brave, that the hatred is reaction formation — is the only time in the full canon Jameson articulates his own defensive structure aloud. Clinically, this is a **single-episode insight event** of remarkable depth. It is also, characteristically, **not integrated**. Within issues he returns to baseline editorializing. The insight was real; the metabolization was not. This is the signature pattern of the man: he can see himself, briefly, in extremis, and then he closes the file.

**Cognitive style.** The 80s show Jameson at his most cognitively flexible. The Stern run depicts him reasoning publicly through Hobgoblin coverage, weighing sources, second-guessing his own editorial impulses on non-Spider-Man matters. He is, at this stage, a genuinely good newspaperman in the daylight portions of his cognition. The Spider-Man module remains walled off, but the wall is now consciously maintained — he knows it is there, which is different from not knowing. The lock is now a door he chooses not to open.

**Self-concept.** The bifurcation widens and stabilizes. Public-Jameson and Private-Jameson are now distinct enough that close witnesses (Robbie, Marla, Peter, Urich) can address either one and Jameson will answer in the appropriate register. This is **functional dissociation**, mild, ego-syntonic, and load-bearing. It is the architecture that keeps him from collapse for the rest of the decade. Without it the Sin-Eater disclosure would have required reorganization he is not equipped to perform.

The marriage also forces a self-concept revision around **lovability**. The 1960s/70s Jameson did not believe he was lovable; he believed he was respectable, which is different. Marla loves him, demonstrably, in the face of all the evidence he himself would marshal against the proposition. The cognitive dissonance is resolved not by accepting lovability but by **protecting the lover** — Marla becomes the only person whose criticism does not produce eruption, because eruption would risk her, and Jameson's threat-detection around Marla is the cleanest signal in his nervous system.

---

## IV. The 1990s — Containment and Drift (DeMatteis/Michelinie/Clone-era, Ages ~70–80)

**Affect regulation.** This decade is, paradoxically, his most stable affectively and his most cognitively stagnant. Marla is present, Robbie is present, the Bugle is solvent (mostly), and the Spider-Man situation has settled into something Jameson has stopped expecting to win and started experiencing as **scenery**. The eruptions continue but they have a perfunctory quality. He yells because that is what he does; he calms because his physiology now demands recovery time at sixty-plus. The cardiovascular load is being managed — pharmacologically (beta-blocker references appear in some Clone Saga continuity), behaviorally (Marla's interventions), and structurally (he delegates more to Robbie).

**Cognitive style.** The drift. Without the existential threat the 60s/70s offered, Jameson's cognition narrows rather than expanding. He does not become wiser in the 90s; he becomes more **rehearsed**. His editorials begin to repeat themselves. The Clone Saga's editorial demand for narrative chaos catches him in a period where his pattern-locking serves the writers more than the character — he is used as a fixed antagonist precisely because he has stopped evolving on his own. Clinically, this is the **calcification phase** common in personalities of this structure entering their eighth decade: the defenses that have worked harden into the only available repertoire, and novelty is processed as threat-or-irrelevant with no third category.

**Self-concept.** Defended and fragile. The 90s Jameson is the most likely to be **wounded by minor provocation** — small slights produce disproportionate retaliation because the self-concept no longer has the youthful buoyancy to absorb them. He sues people more. He fires people more (and rehires them — the Betty Brant pattern). The grandiosity is now maintenance-grandiosity: it requires daily renewal through subordinate compliance, masthead presence, and ritualized morning humiliation of whichever staffer is closest. The shame substrate is closer to the surface than in any prior decade, which is why the trigger threshold has dropped.

---

## V. The 2000s — Reckonings (Straczynski/Bendis/*Civil War*, Ages ~80–85)

**Affect regulation.** The decade of the **somatic bill**. The Bendis *Pulse* myocardial infarction is the watershed: Gargan, as Venom, confronts Jameson with the fact of his own authorship, and Jameson's cardiovascular system arrests. This is not coincidence and the writing does not treat it as coincidence. The body delivers the verdict the conscious mind has refused for forty years of in-universe time. Post-MI Jameson is a different affective creature: the volume is intact, but the **recovery curve is longer**. Eruptions now leave him visibly drained. He sits down more. He sweats more. He acknowledges, in private moments with Marla and occasionally Robbie, that he is tired.

The Civil War period adds a second layer: the **unmasking of Spider-Man** (in the original 2006 sequence, pre-One-More-Day) produces in Jameson a response that is clinically diagnostic. He does not feel vindicated; he feels **betrayed**, and the betrayal is structured exactly like the paternal betrayal of his childhood — *the man I trusted was a fraud operating in concealment*. The lawsuit against Peter is petty on its surface and tectonic underneath: it is an attempt to restage the original injury with himself in the position of authority and the deceiver punished. The affect, in the panels where he files, is not satisfaction but something closer to a child's outrage finally given a legal instrument.

**Cognitive style.** The walls between modules begin to leak. Post-MI Jameson cannot maintain the bifurcation as cleanly. The Spider-Man module starts contaminating the editorial-discipline module, and the editorial-discipline module starts contaminating the Spider-Man module. He is by turns more reasonable about Spider-Man and less reasonable about everything else. This is the cognitive signature of an aging, post-cardiac personality whose defensive economy is no longer adequately funded.

**Self-concept.** First major revision since the marriage. The MI inserts mortality as a fact rather than a rhetorical flourish. He begins, very tentatively, to assess his life as **finite and assessable**. He does not like the assessment. The grandiosity acquires a wistful underside — he speaks more about the Bugle's history, his father (still in pre-revelation form for most of this decade), the city as it was. The self-concept is becoming **retrospective**, which is new and which is the precondition for everything that happens in the next decade.

---

## VI. The 2010s — Catastrophe, Reorientation, and the Hardest Update (Slott era, Ages ~85–90)

**Affect regulation.** The mayoral period (Slott, "Brand New Day" through "Spider-Island") shows Jameson's affective system under maximum institutional load. Governance suits his temperament worse than publishing: a publisher can pick fights, but a mayor must absorb them. He is bad at this. The eruptions during the mayoralty are visibly costlier, his staff turnover is high, and the FACT/Anti-Spider Squad obsession is the most expensive expression of his Spider-Man fixation to date because it is now drawing on public funds and public accountability.

Then **Marla is killed** (Spider-Island/Smythe revenge). The clinical event is total. The affective regulator he had relied on since the mid-80s is removed in a single sequence, and Jameson does not have a backup. The grief is not depicted as grief in any conventional register — there is no extended depressive arc, no weeping sequence, no breakdown. Instead there is **dissociated functioning**: he resigns, he disappears from the masthead, he returns thinner and quieter, he speaks of Marla in flat sentences, he does not metabolize. This is grief in a personality that has no instrument for grief. It expresses as **subtraction** rather than emotion — a quantity of Jameson is simply gone, and the remainder is harder.

**Cognitive style.** The **unmasking** (Spencer, ~2018–19) is the cognitive event of the decade and arguably of his life. Peter, voluntarily, tells him. Jameson is not given the satisfaction of catching him; he is given the more difficult gift of being trusted with the truth. The processing is slow, awkward, and observable across multiple arcs. He moves through:

1. **Rage** — predictable, brief, exhausted faster than prior rages because the body cannot sustain them.
2. **Retrospective re-cognition** — a re-reading of every prior interaction, panel-flashbacks that are explicitly Jameson's, not the narrator's. He is doing the work in real time.
3. **Overcorrection** — the podcasting, the public advocacy, the lurches into hagiography. This is the same reaction-formation engine running in reverse: he cannot occupy a middle position; he can only flip polarity.
4. **Halting integration** — the late-Spencer scenes where he speaks to Peter about Ben Parker, where he acknowledges, obliquely, the cost. The apology that never quite arrives in the proportion the harm requires, but the changed behavior that does.

This is, clinically, **a personality update of the maximum magnitude this structure can perform**. It is incomplete. It is also more than the literature on this kind of personality typically predicts. The man can change. He is exceptionally costly to change. He changed.

**Self-concept.** Re-bifurcated, then partially re-fused on new terms. The public-Jameson is now uncertain — the podcast voice is not the editorial voice; it is searching, sometimes pleading, sometimes funny in ways the editorial Jameson never permitted himself to be. The private-Jameson is, for the first time, the **older one** — the one with more authority — because the public-Jameson has lost his platforms and his certainties. The self that Marla loved becomes, posthumously, the self he tries to be. He is not always successful.

---

## VII. The 2020s — Reversion, Residue, and the Final Architecture (Various, Ages ~90+)

**Affect regulation.** Event-driven volatility returns in post-Spencer runs, but the baseline has shifted. He is quieter between eruptions. The recovery time is longer still. He has been taught, by Marla's absence and the MI and the unmasking, that his body will not indefinitely subsidize his temperament, and there is evidence (cigar reduction, on-panel medication, more frequent seated postures) that he has accepted this in a way the 1980s Jameson would not have.

**Cognitive style.** The **pattern-lock relapses** under event-driven writing pressure are real and consistent with the etiology: under sufficient ambient threat, Jameson's nervous system reaches for the oldest available organizing principle, which is *find the masked man and expose him*. This is not character regression in the dismissive sense; it is **trauma-response reversion**, predictable under stress in any personality of this developmental history. The capacity for update demonstrated in the 2010s is not lost; it is **expensive to access**, and in cheap-cognition moments he reaches for the older tool.

**Self-concept.** The final architecture is a man who knows what he is, refuses to be only that, and fails at the refusal often enough to suffer. The grandiosity is now intermittent and almost performative — he reaches for it as a tool rather than living inside it. The shame substrate is closer to the surface than it has ever been, which makes him, paradoxically, **easier to be around in small doses and harder in large ones**. The Sin-Eater disclosure, never fully metabolized, has nonetheless seeded a continuous low-grade self-awareness that the 1960s Jameson did not possess and could not have tolerated.

---

## VIII. The Three Lines, Read Together

**Affect regulation** moves from un-mediated reactivity (60s) → first wariness (70s) → co-regulated stability (80s) → calcified maintenance (90s) → somatic verdict and grief-subtraction (00s–10s) → costly, body-rationed modulation (20s). The arc is not toward serenity; it is toward **economy** — a man whose nervous system has been forced to budget what it once spent freely.

**Cognitive style** moves from rapid, locked, target-blind (60s) → first documented update (70s) → walled flexibility (80s) → calcification (90s) → leakage between modules (00s) → maximum-magnitude update under the unmasking (10s) → stressed reversion with retained capacity (20s). The arc is toward **fragile pluralism** — a mind that has more positions available than it used to, but reaches for the oldest one when tired.

**Self-concept** moves from un-shamed grandiosity (60s) → first micro-fractures (70s) → functional bifurcation (80s) → defended fragility (90s) → retrospective assessment (00s) → re-bifurcation and partial re-fusion on new terms (10s) → intermittent, almost performative grandiosity over an exposed shame substrate (20s). The arc is toward **honesty he did not choose and cannot fully bear** — which is, in this clinical structure, the closest thing to growth the personality can produce.

The wound — paternal abuse, paternal fraud, a powerful man in concealment who hurt people and got away with it — is the constant. Every decade is a different instrument played on the same string. What changes is the player's awareness that the string is there. In the 1960s he did not know. In the 2010s he knew and could not always act on the knowing. That gap, narrowing over sixty years and never closing, is the longitudinal psychological profile of John Jonah Jameson, Jr.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: John Jonah Jameson, Jr.
### Section 5 of UATU Dossier Compilation

---

## 5.0 Framing Note and Methodological Caveat

This section attempts a formal diagnostic formulation of a subject who has never, to the documentary record's knowledge, sat for a structured clinical interview. The DSM-5-TR and ICD-11 criteria invoked below are applied to a sixty-year longitudinal behavioral record assembled from public conduct, sworn testimony in civil and federal matters, contemporaneous reporting (including the subject's own bylined editorials and on-camera podcasts, which together constitute one of the largest self-corpora available for any living American non-academic), and the testimonies of those who have worked alongside him for decades — chief among them Robertson, Brant, Urich, and, latterly and most consequentially, Parker.

The subject is functioning. He has run a major metropolitan newspaper for the better part of forty years, completed a full mayoral term of New York City, sustained a second professional life as a podcaster and broadcast personality, and remained married, until widowed, to a credentialed scientist who is by all accounts not a fool about men. Whatever the file contains, it does not contain the kind of decompensation that requires custodial care. The diagnostic question is therefore one of **structure and characterology**, not of acute illness.

A high-functioning subject is the hardest kind to formulate, because every diagnostic signal is partially masked by the compensations that have made the functioning possible. The Bugle is, among other things, Jameson's prosthesis. So is the cigar. So is the bark.

---

## 5.1 Primary Formulation

### 5.1.1 Headline

**Pathological Narcissism, vulnerable-predominant subtype with grandiose surface, embedded in a developmental trauma substrate (childhood physical abuse, paternal antisocial/fraudulent modeling), with secondary chronic stress pathology of significant somatic burden and an episodic anger-dyscontrol pattern that does not meet full criteria for a discrete impulse-control disorder but is operationally indistinguishable from it in workplace and political settings.**

This is the spine. Everything below either elaborates, comorbidly attaches to, or is differentially excluded from this formulation.

### 5.1.2 Why "features," not "disorder"

The published record disqualifies a clean Narcissistic Personality Disorder diagnosis in the full DSM-5-TR sense for one reason that recurs across every era of canon: **the man can love and be loyal, and has done so durably across decades.** Marla Madison-Jameson was not a narcissistic supply; she was a wife to whom he deferred in private and whose death he has not metabolized. Robertson is not a sycophant; he is the conscience to whom Jameson grants veto authority on the masthead and whose moral standing Jameson defends at personal cost (the Tombstone frame-up arc; the post-Civil War rehabilitations). Urich, Brant, his son John — these are not mirrors. They are people whose autonomy Jameson recognizes, often grudgingly, and whose welfare he protects, often clumsily.

NPD-proper requires a pervasive pattern of grandiosity, need for admiration, and **lack of empathy**, present across contexts. Jameson's empathy is selective, deferred, and badly expressed — but it is present, sustained, and acts on his behavior. The diagnosis must therefore degrade to **Pathological Narcissism, vulnerable-predominant subtype**, a Pincus/Levy-tradition construct that better captures the **shame-driven, hypersensitive, contempt-armored** clinical picture the file actually shows. He is not the cold, exploitative narcissist of the prototype. He is the wounded narcissist who **must always be the one who saw the truth first**, whose grandiose displays are compensatory rather than primary, and whose collapses (post-Marla; post-mayoral resignation; the MI in the Bendis arc) are characteristically vulnerable-type implosions — withdrawal, somatization, shame — rather than grandiose-type rages externalized without internal cost.

### 5.1.3 Symptom Mapping to DSM-5-TR NPD Criteria

Working through the nine criteria with evidence:

1. **Grandiose sense of self-importance.** *Present, moderate.* Masthead positioning, editorial first-person, mayoral self-mythology, podcast brand built on his name. Tempered by genuine accomplishment (a real newspaper, a real elected term) which makes the grandiosity reality-anchored rather than purely confabulated.
2. **Preoccupation with fantasies of unlimited success/power/brilliance.** *Subclinical.* He is more often preoccupied with deficits than with fantasies. He worries about the paper folding, about being scooped, about being made a fool of. This is vulnerable-subtype texture, not grandiose-subtype texture.
3. **Belief in being "special" and unique.** *Present, in journalistic register only.* He believes in his nose, his sources, his instincts. He does not believe he is generically superior; he believes he is correct.
4. **Need for excessive admiration.** *Present and chronic.* The masthead, the editorials, the cigar-pointing in conference rooms, the podcast's parasocial dynamic. The admiration he craves is, tellingly, **agreement** — not adoration. He wants to be right out loud.
5. **Sense of entitlement.** *Present, situationally.* Operates as if owed deference within his own institutions; markedly less entitled in venues he does not control (federal hearings; meetings with the Mayor's Office during others' administrations; family gatherings with Marla's people).
6. **Interpersonally exploitative.** *Partial.* He uses people, but he pays them, defends them, and frequently overcompensates when the exploitation becomes visible to him (the famous freelance underpayment of Parker is real, but so is the bail money, the hospital visits, the legal cover when staff are in trouble). The exploitation is structural and habitual rather than predatory.
7. **Lack of empathy.** *Partial and selective.* He is empathically blind toward Spider-Man specifically (and toward masked vigilantes generically), and empathically clumsy toward people in real time. Across distance, in writing, and toward known individuals, empathy is functional. **This is the criterion that most clearly fails for full NPD.**
8. **Envy of others / belief others envy him.** *Strongly present.* Spider-Man is the envy object par excellence. So, in subtler form, are heroic public figures generally, war correspondents who go to the front, anyone who pays a body-cost for what he pays only a money-and-rage cost for. The Sin-Eater confession (Peter David, *Spectacular Spider-Man* #107–110) is, clinically, an envy-disclosure.
9. **Arrogant, haughty behaviors.** *Surface-level and persistent.* The persona. Largely armor.

**Six clean hits, two partials, one fail.** That is features-level. Sufficient to anchor the formulation, insufficient to call full NPD without distortion.

### 5.1.4 Etiological Account

The vulnerable narcissism is **trauma-derived, not constitutional.** The published origin material — the Waid/Slott-era backstory establishing John Jonah Jameson, Sr. as a domestic abuser, conman, and bigamist whose secondary family surfaced in Jonah's adulthood — provides the developmental template with unusual completeness. Three mechanisms must be noted:

- **Identification with the aggressor.** The bark, the desk-pounding, the use of institutional power to compel deference — these are the father's affect modulation strategies in a son who consciously rejected the father. The form survives where the content is repudiated.
- **Counter-identification as moral project.** The crusading-publisher self is the deliberately constructed negation of the father. Where Jameson, Sr. lied for personal gain, Jameson, Jr. *prints the truth even at cost.* This is a real ethical achievement and the source of his civic value.
- **Hypervigilance for the hidden.** A child raised by a man whose public face concealed a private criminal develops, structurally and durably, an alarm system tuned to **the gap between presentation and reality.** Adult Jameson's mask-hatred is the symptom-level expression of this hypervigilance. Spider-Man — a powerful man in concealment — is a perfect stimulus. The hatred is not about Parker. It was waiting for somebody.

Add the maternal record: insufficiently protective, by the canonical accounting. This produces, in the textbook way, an adult who **cannot trust caregivers to protect him from the powerful** and who therefore must **become the powerful** to ensure his own safety. The publisher's chair is the safe seat. The mayoralty was the next safe seat. The podcast is the smaller safe seat he built when the others were taken away.

---

## 5.2 Comorbid Conditions

### 5.2.1 Chronic Stress / Somatic Symptom Pathology

**ICD-11: 6C20 Bodily distress disorder, moderate, with cardiovascular and gastrointestinal focus.** The peptic ulcer disease antedates the Spider-Man obsession by the testimony of the earliest issues themselves; antacids and physician warnings are textual from the Lee era forward. Hypertension is undocumented in formal lab values within the public record but operationally certain from observed flushing, vein prominence under affect, near-syncopal episodes following outbursts, and the eventual confirmed myocardial infarction during the Venom-Gargan confrontation (Bendis, *The Pulse*).

The pattern is classical: **affect generated, affect refused, affect routed to viscera.** Jameson is a man whose autonomic nervous system performs the emotional processing his consciousness will not. The MI is the single most diagnostically useful event in the file because it places a date on the bill for the 1964 Stillwell/Gargan decision and on the larger habit of converting psychological cost into cardiovascular cost.

### 5.2.2 Intermittent Anger Dyscontrol

**Subthreshold for Intermittent Explosive Disorder (DSM-5-TR 312.34) by frequency-of-aggression criteria, but only because his aggression is overwhelmingly verbal and his physical assaults on property (the famous desk-pounding, the cigars hurled, the staplers thrown in two documented instances) are infrequent and never directed at persons.**

The episodes are real, stereotyped, and disproportionate. Trigger → escalation to florid verbal aggression within seconds → peak with object-displacement or door-slamming → rapid de-escalation → return to functional state with mild dysphoria and no apparent pleasure in the aftermath. The absence of post-episode satisfaction is diagnostically important — it distinguishes this pattern from sadistic or antisocial aggression and aligns it with stress-driven dyscontrol in a temperamentally irritable individual.

Best classified as **Anger Dyscontrol, episodic, secondary to personality structure and chronic stress load.**

### 5.2.3 Complicated / Prolonged Grief

**ICD-11: 6B42 Prolonged Grief Disorder, partial, in remission with anniversary reactivation.** Marla Madison-Jameson's death during the Spider-Island/Smythe-revenge sequence has not been processed within normative timeframes. The record shows avoidance of her name in non-essential contexts, intrusive reactivation during stress, marked anhedonia in the months following the event, and a re-engagement with public life (the podcast era) that has the structure of activity-as-distraction rather than restored equilibrium. Compounded by the brutal irony of the agent (a Spider-Slayer descendant — the lineage he himself funded), the grief is **shame-contaminated**, which is the most treatment-resistant variant.

### 5.2.4 Persistent Adjustment Reaction to the Unmasking

Not a formal diagnosis. Worth flagging. The post-unmasking arc shows a sustained reorganization of self-concept that has the texture of a slow-motion adjustment reaction to a singular disconfirming event. Initial rage, prolonged disorganization, the awkward overcorrection into Spider-Man podcast advocacy, the inability to apologize in proportion, the late-period drift back toward antagonism under writerly pressure — these are the recognizable phases of a partially-integrated update to a load-bearing belief. He is still adjusting. He may always be adjusting.

### 5.2.5 Tobacco Use Disorder, in sustained remission

Decades of heavy cigar use, reduced after the cardiac event, eliminated by the late mayoral period in most canonical accounts. Replacement behaviors visible (gesture, gum, oral fixation transferred to the prop-cigar he sometimes holds unlit during broadcasts). Standard course; unremarkable but for the symbolic weight of the cigar in his interpersonal arsenal.

### 5.2.6 What Is *Not* Comorbid

- **No substance use disorder** beyond the tobacco. Conspicuously **not** a drinker by his industry's standards; the file lacks the bar-soaked editor cliché that would have been the easy characterization.
- **No diagnosable depressive disorder** outside the bereavement window. His baseline is irritable, not anhedonic.
- **No anxiety disorder** in the symptom-cluster sense. He is hypervigilant, but the vigilance is ego-syntonic, productively channeled into journalism, and not phenomenologically experienced as anxiety. He would be insulted by the suggestion, which is itself diagnostic.

---

## 5.3 Course Over Time

The longitudinal trajectory is more stable than dramatic — a defining feature of personality pathology rather than acute illness.

- **Era 1 (1963–1975, Lee/Romita/Conway).** Symptomatology florid and uninterrupted. Grandiose surface dominant. Anger dyscontrol at lifetime peak. Ulcer present and active. Reaction formation against Spider-Man at maximum operational expression (Stillwell/Gargan commissioning; first-person Smythe-Slayer piloting). No insight.
- **Era 2 (1975–1987, Wein/Stern/DeFalco).** Stable. Marriage to Marla introduces the first sustained interpersonal data showing intact attachment capacity. Sin-Eater era produces the first significant insight disclosure. Sublimation channel matures; civic-journalist identity consolidates as a real and stable second self.
- **Era 3 (1987–2004, post-Stern through pre-Bendis).** Maintenance. Same patterns; the John Jameson lycanthropy/transformation arcs repeatedly demonstrate that paternal attachment overrides ideological rigidity under sufficient threat. Cardiovascular load accruing silently.
- **Era 4 (2004–2008, Bendis/*Pulse*, Civil War).** **First major somatic decompensation (MI).** Civil War clarifies and exposes the opportunism layered beneath the principled façade (the Parker lawsuit). Pre-collapse phase of late life begins.
- **Era 5 (2008–2011, Slott mayoralty).** Acting-out via expanded institutional power. The same personality given larger toys. Culminates in Marla's death — **the second major decompensation**, this time affective rather than somatic. Resignation. Withdrawal.
- **Era 6 (post-mayoralty through unmasking, 2011–2018).** Reduced operational scale. Podcast era. The wound from Marla's death is not closed. Late-life narrowing of life-space, characteristic of vulnerable narcissism in the seventh decade.
- **Era 7 (unmasking forward, 2018–present).** The cognitive event he has spent his life structurally avoiding finally arrives. Slow, incomplete reorganization. Genuine behavioral change against a substrate that still tries to rebound to its prior shape. The capacity for update is **proven**, the rate is **slow**, and the regression-under-stress is **predictable**. He will die updating.

The arc is the arc of a personality that has worked at full operating cost for sixty years and is now paying interest on the loan. He is not deteriorating in the sense of cognitive decline; the public record shows preserved verbal intelligence, memory, and decisional capacity. He is *settling* — the compensations are getting more visible because the energy to hide them is dwindling.

---

## 5.4 Differential — What He Is *Not*

This is where most lay diagnosticians of the subject have erred.

### 5.4.1 Not Antisocial Personality Disorder

The temptation is real: he funded the creation of a supervillain, weaponized his newspaper for personal vendetta, sued the man whose photographs built his paper, used the mayoral office to pursue a private fixation. Surface-read: antisocial.

**Disqualifying evidence is decisive.**
- **Conscience present and active.** The Scorpion guilt has been textually disclosed across multiple writers, multiple decades, and surfaces somatically (the *Pulse* MI was triggered by the Gargan confrontation precisely because the encounter named his original sin). Antisocial subjects do not somatize their crimes.
- **No pattern of unlawful behavior outside the Spider-Man fixation.** He pays his taxes. He honors contracts. He refuses bribes that would solve real cash-flow problems (multiple Kingpin-era stories).
- **Loyalty to non-utilitarian relationships.** Robertson, Brant, Urich, Marla, John, eventually Parker. ASPD subjects do not sustain decades-long loyalty bonds with people who are not currently useful to them.
- **Remorse, deferred but real.** The post-unmasking arc would be incoherent under an ASPD formulation; an antisocial subject would simply reframe and continue.

### 5.4.2 Not Paranoid Personality Disorder

His suspicion is **targeted and reality-anchored**, not diffuse. He trusts a stable, narrow circle for decades. PPD requires pervasive distrust without sufficient basis; Jameson's distrust is hyper-specific (masks; concealed power; his father's archetype) and demonstrably permeable to evidence outside the trigger category. He has been wrong about Spider-Man for thirty years; he has been right about the Kingpin, Norman Osborn-in-political-life, and a long roster of municipal corruptions. A PPD subject would not have that hit rate. Pattern-locked overvalued ideation against a specific stimulus class is not paranoia.

### 5.4.3 Not Delusional Disorder

Persecutory or grandiose delusions are by definition fixed and impermeable to disconfirming evidence. Jameson's Spider-Man fixation **has been demonstrated to update** under the cumulative weight of decades of evidence and the singular event of the unmasking. Slow, partial, painful update is incompatible with delusion. What he has is **a load-bearing overvalued idea** in the Wernicke/McKenna sense — affectively saturated, identity-organizing, ego-syntonic, but in principle revisable. The post-unmasking behavioral change is the diagnostic test, and the test favors overvalued ideation, not delusion.

### 5.4.4 Not Bipolar Spectrum

No documented manic or hypomanic episodes by criterion (sustained mood elevation, decreased need for sleep, grandiosity outside baseline, pressured speech as a *change* from premorbid). His high-energy states are situational (deadline; crisis; campaign) and his low-energy states are reactive (Marla; MI recovery). Mood is dysregulated within a narrow irritable-baseline band, not cycled across poles. The persistent loud-and-fast presentation is a stable trait, not an episodic state.

### 5.4.5 Not Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder

He is messy. His desk is famously chaotic. His decision-making is fast and intuition-led, not rule-bound. He delegates (badly, abrasively, but extensively). OCPD subjects are perfectionistic, rigid about procedure, and miserly. Jameson is rigid about *targets and conclusions*, not procedures, and he is financially generous to his loyalty circle even while underpaying freelancers as a matter of business habit. The rigidity is content-rigidity, not structure-rigidity.

### 5.4.6 Not Histrionic Personality Disorder

The flamboyance is real but **purpose-built for institutional dominance**, not for attention or seduction. He does not require admiration from rooms in which he has no operational stake. He is not theatrical with strangers. The cigar, the volume, the office choreography are *display behaviors for the home court*, switched off in venues that do not matter to him.

### 5.4.7 Not PTSD, formal

Despite the abusive childhood and the multiple kidnapping/hostage events, the file does not show the characteristic intrusion/avoidance/hyperarousal triad in a discrete syndromal pattern. What it shows is **complex developmental trauma absorbed into character structure** — the personality is the symptom. The hypervigilance is ego-syntonic; the avoidance is conceptual (don't think about father, don't think about Stillwell, don't think about Marla) rather than phobic; the intrusion is sublimated into editorial production. This is closer to **ICD-11 Complex PTSD without the affective dysregulation criterion fully met** — call it **subsyndromal cPTSD with personality-level integration**.

### 5.4.8 Not Adult ADHD

The propulsive, rapid-fire cognitive style is sometimes lay-labeled as ADHD. Disqualifying: sustained attention to long-form journalistic and political projects across decades, organizational capacity to run a newsroom and a mayoralty, no documented executive-function failures outside emotional dysregulation. The speed is temperamental, not attentional.

### 5.4.9 Not Major Depressive Disorder

The post-Marla period shows grief, not depression. The post-MI period shows convalescence, not anhedonia. The post-mayoral resignation shows narcissistic injury, not melancholia. He has never gone dark in the clinical sense. Irritable baseline is not depressive baseline.

### 5.4.10 Not Full Vulnerable Narcissism Either

A note of internal precision. The pure vulnerable narcissist is socially withdrawn, hypersensitive in private, and avoidant of competitive display. Jameson **runs toward** the public arena. The vulnerable subtype best describes his **interior weather**; his **exterior weather** is grandiose. The integrated picture is what the contemporary literature calls **the oscillating narcissist** — vulnerable inside, grandiose outside, with the gap between the two doing most of the symptomatic work. The Sin-Eater confession is the precise moment when the gap becomes briefly conscious to the subject.

---

## 5.5 Integrated Formulation Statement

The subject is a sixty-plus-year-old male with **trauma-derived oscillating pathological narcissism, vulnerable-predominant internally, grandiose-presented externally,** carrying a heavy **somatic stress load** (status-post myocardial infarction; long-standing peptic ulcer disease; presumed hypertension) and a stable **episodic anger-dyscontrol pattern** that does not meet full IED criteria. He carries **subsyndromal complex PTSD** from documented paternal physical abuse and the later disclosure of paternal antisocial/fraudulent behavior


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — J. JONAH JAMESON, JR.

*Subsection 6 of the UATU Dossier. Granular catalog of observable behavior, micro-tells, and decision habits across the full affective and situational range. Drawn from sixty years of canonical observation and inferred from the longitudinal somatic-behavioral record established in §§1–5. Surveillance-grade detail: what a continuous-watch file would record about the man if every minute of his day for forty years had been logged.*

---

## 6.0 Baseline — The Resting Jameson

There is no true "calm" Jameson in the operational record; there is only **idle**, which still runs at an arousal level most adults would call agitated. The baseline is what a continuous monitor would show during ordinary office hours when nothing has gone wrong.

**Postural baseline.** Sits forward, never back. Even in his own executive chair, the lumbar contact is intermittent; the weight is on the forearms, elbows planted, torso pitched fifteen to twenty degrees toward whatever is on the desk. When he does lean back it is performative — a deliberate shift to signal "I am about to dismiss you" or "I am about to deliver a verdict." Subordinates learn to read the recline as a punctuation mark, not a relaxation.

**Hand baseline.** Right hand to cigar (or, post-cardiac, to an unlit cigar held like a cigar; the prop persists after the substance is curtailed). Left hand free for paper, phone, jabbing. He does not idle his hands. If both are empty for more than four or five seconds he reaches for something — pen, lighter, the lip of a coffee cup, the corner of a manuscript — and begins to manipulate it. The fidget is constant and is part of how he thinks; interrupting it (snatching the cigar away, removing the desk) makes him visibly worse, not better.

**Vocal baseline.** Mid-chest projection at all times, even one-on-one. He does not have an indoor voice; he has volumes of outdoor voice. In dictation or solo work he subvocalizes audibly — sentences for editorials are tested aloud before they reach paper. The cadence is staccato with abrupt downshifts: short bursts, hard stops, then a muttered coda half a beat later that no one is supposed to fully hear but everyone does.

**Ocular baseline.** Hard, fast scanning. Eyes track to motion before they track to people; he registers the door, the window, the elevator indicator, the bullpen floor through the glass before he registers the face of the person in front of him. This is a vigilance pattern, not a discourtesy, and it is consistent with the abuse-derived hyperarousal mapped in §3.

**Facial baseline.** The brow is the diagnostic instrument. It is never neutral. At rest the corrugators are engaged; the resting expression is a low-grade scowl that observers misread as displeasure but which is actually concentration. When genuine displeasure arrives the brow does not go further down — it goes *forward*, the orbital ridge tilting into the field of vision like a visor.

**Gait baseline.** Walks the Bugle bullpen on a circuit. The route is consistent across decades and across editors who have tried to relocate his office: door of his office → city desk → photo desk → copy → back along the windows → return. Six minutes if uninterrupted; he is almost never uninterrupted. Subordinates time their approaches to intercept him on the photo-desk leg, which is empirically when he is most receptive (he is closest to the visual evidence and the cigar smoke has dispersed enough to allow eye contact).

**Olfactory and territorial baseline.** Smoke as territory. The office, pre-cardiac, was a column of stale cigar that extended into the hallway and made the room legible by smell from the elevator. Post-cardiac, the residue persists in the carpet, the curtains, the upholstery, and the man himself; the office still smells of him even when he has been out for days. He has never decorated personally — every framed item on the wall is either a Bugle front page, a civic award, or a photograph of John in flight gear. There are no images of his father. There is, in the desk drawer (third down, left side, by report and by inference from his hand habits when stressed), a photo of his mother and a separate one of Marla.

---

## 6.1 Calm — The Working State

True calm is a rumor. What functions as calm is **absorbed work**, and it has its own profile.

When the page is closing and the copy is good, the volume drops by half. The cigar is held but not actively chewed. He reads with the page tilted ten degrees up, a pencil tracking the lines. He underlines, never highlights. He marks queries in the margin with a small Greek *delta* — change — that no one taught him and that has appeared in his marginalia continuously since the Lee era. When the read is going well, his lips move and there is a faint nodding cadence at sentence ends, like a metronome confirming that the prose is working.

In absorbed work, **he forgets the door**. People can enter without being barked at. Robbie Robertson learned this decades ago and exploits it to deliver bad news during page-close, when Jameson's working calm absorbs the impact better than any other state.

He hums during calm. Always the same handful of tunes — march-era and big-band stuff from the era of his early adulthood, half-remembered and tuneless. The humming is unconscious; it stops the instant he notices it, then resumes within ninety seconds.

His handwriting in calm is upright, small, and surprisingly neat — the print of a man who learned penmanship in a 1940s classroom and never let it slip. The handwriting in stress, by contrast, slopes hard right and grows by a third in size; the difference is so reliable that an experienced secretary could pre-sort his memos by mood from the slant alone.

He drinks coffee in calm. He drinks more coffee in stress. The cup is the same chipped mug for a thirty-year stretch in the canonical record; replacement was actively resisted on at least two documented occasions.

---

## 6.2 Mild Irritation — The Default Weather

This is the state most people who meet Jameson encounter and mistake for his personality. It is not. It is the friction layer over the working state and it has a predictable choreography.

**The jab.** The cigar comes out of the mouth and points. It points at the subordinate, at the page, at the door, at the city through the window. Each jab is a syllable; the cigar is a baton beating time for the rant. Observers who have logged him long enough can count beats per minute and correlate to severity.

**The repetition.** He repeats the offending noun three times with rising stress. "Pictures, Parker — pictures, *pictures*." The triplication is unconscious and diagnostic; it appears only in mild-to-moderate irritation and disappears at higher stress (where he becomes more, not less, syntactically organized).

**The pivot to a third party.** Mild irritation almost always recruits an audience. He will turn from the offender to Robbie or to the bullpen at large — *"Listen to this, he wants —"* — to make the offense public. This is reaction formation in real time: the audience converts a personal feeling into a civic case.

**The non-firing firing.** "You're fired, Parker." Said an order of magnitude more often than enacted. The threat is ritual; it is how he ends a transaction that has frustrated him without having to acknowledge the frustration. Subordinates who have been "fired" more than three times in a year are, paradoxically, in the inner circle; they are family enough to bear the discharge of affect.

**The walk-out and walk-back.** He will eject a subordinate, then within ten minutes find a reason to summon them back without comment on the ejection. Continuity is restored by act, never by apology. This is the single most consistent interpersonal pattern in the entire file.

---

## 6.3 Moderate Stress — The Editorial State

When the day has gone wrong but the body is still holding, the personality reorganizes around the editorial voice. He becomes more articulate, not less; the syntax tightens; the vocabulary climbs a register. He writes better when he is angry, and he knows it, and the knowing is itself part of the engine.

**Pacing.** The bullpen circuit doubles in frequency and shortens in radius. He no longer reaches the windows; he stops at the city desk and pivots. Subordinates learn to clear the corridor.

**Phone behavior.** He picks up on the first ring and identifies himself by surname only, last name barked. He does not say goodbye; the call ends when he has obtained or delivered what he needed. The receiver is replaced with controlled force — never slammed in this state; slamming is reserved for §6.4.

**Decision habits.** Faster, narrower, more committed. He stops soliciting opinion and starts issuing it. Robbie, who has the longest empirical record of managing this state, has a documented technique: he agrees with the *frame* of Jameson's position while adjusting the *facts* inside it. ("You're right we need to hit this hard, boss — here's the angle that won't get us sued.") This works approximately seventy percent of the time and is the closest thing the Bugle has to a constitutional check.

**Somatic tells.** The vein at the left temple becomes visible. The complexion reddens from the collar up. He reaches for the antacid bottle in the second-right desk drawer and chews two tablets without water; the chewing is audible and is itself a warning sign to anyone within earshot. The cigar is bitten through with greater frequency in this state — staff have noted multiple cigars discarded mid-length on days of moderate stress.

**The editorial as discharge.** He will produce twelve hundred words of furious copy in one sitting and emerge measurably calmer. The page is the relief valve. Deny him the page (vacation, illness, the period of his mayoralty when he was supposed to stay out of the Bugle's editorial decisions) and the moderate stress does not resolve — it climbs.

---

## 6.4 High Stress — The Pre-Collapse Window

When the editorial discharge is not enough — when the story is breaking against him, when a libel suit lands, when Marla's bills come in alongside a Slayer attack, when the Scorpion is on the loose — the state changes character.

**Volume increases but consonants degrade.** He is now shouting, but the diction loses precision. Sentences abandon halfway. The repetition pattern from §6.2 expands from three to four and five — the noun is hammered until the rhythm itself substitutes for argument.

**Loss of the audience instinct.** In moderate stress he plays to the room. In high stress he forgets it. He will say things in front of the wrong people that he would never say in moderate stress; this is the window in which his deepest fears about himself leak (the cowardice confession to Peter during the Sin-Eater arc occurred in exactly this register).

**The cigar is dropped or forgotten.** A reliable marker. If the cigar is on the desk unattended and unlit, the stress has crossed into the pre-collapse band.

**Errors of judgment cluster here.** The decision to fund Smythe's first Slayer; the commission of Stillwell's mutagenic procedure on Gargan; the lawsuit against Peter Parker post-unmasking. The catastrophic decisions in the file are not made in moderate stress (where he writes editorials) or in crisis (where he becomes briefly clear); they are made in this narrow band where the body is screaming and the mind is still trying to act decisively. **Strategic implication for any handler: never let him make a consequential decision in this state.** Delay it by any means available.

**Somatic warnings.** Diaphoresis at the hairline. Left arm rubbing — unconscious, intermittent. He sits down without intending to and then stands again as though embarrassed by the sitting. The antacids come out a second time within an hour. The complexion goes from red to mottled.

---

## 6.5 Somatic Collapse — The Body Cashing the Check

The bills documented in §2 (ulcer flares, hypertensive episodes, the confirmed MI during the Gargan/Venom confrontation) arrive in a stereotyped sequence.

**Phase one: the freeze.** He stops mid-sentence, hand to chest or to the desk edge. The face does not show alarm; it shows a kind of irritated puzzlement, as though the body is being insubordinate.

**Phase two: denial in motion.** He waves people off. *"I'm fine — get out — fine."* He will try to resume what he was doing. This phase has lasted, by report, from thirty seconds to several minutes; it is the window in which staff who know him override his refusal and call medical.

**Phase three: collapse or near-collapse.** Knees, then chair, then floor in the worst cases. He does not lose consciousness gracefully; observers report him still trying to issue instructions as awareness narrows.

**Phase four (post-event): shame.** This is the most important and least photographed phase. In recovery he is unusually quiet, almost courteous. He thanks the people who helped — once, briefly, without making eye contact. He does not want visitors. Marla was the exception; she was permitted in the room without performance, and his behavior with her in hospital settings (when canonically observed) is the most affectively naked record in the file.

---

## 6.6 Crisis-Grade Threat — The Paradoxical Clearing

The single most counterintuitive finding in the longitudinal record: when actual physical danger arrives — armed men in the lobby, a Slayer in the building, a mob lieutenant across the desk with a contract — Jameson stabilizes. The middle bands of his arousal curve are where he is dangerous to himself and others; the top of the curve is where he is at his best.

**Vocal change.** Volume drops. He speaks at conversational level, sometimes lower. The staccato gives way to complete sentences. Observers consistently describe a "different man."

**Postural change.** He squares to the threat. The forward lean of baseline becomes a stand; if seated, he plants both feet flat and the hands go to the desk, palms down. There is no flinch reflex in his record at this state. He has been physically struck, held at gunpoint, suspended out a window — the gross motor response is to face it.

**Cognitive change.** Decisions in crisis are made slowly and with reference to principle rather than appetite. The Kingpin confrontations, the refusal of mob bribes, the decision to print stories that placed him personally at risk — all made in this state. He cites the First Amendment in this state without irony; in other states he weaponizes it.

**Why.** Per §3, this is consistent with a trauma developmental history in which danger was *clarifying* and the chronic harm lived in ambiguity. The crisis-state Jameson is the child who finally got to see the fist coming and could brace. The instinct that would be dysfunctional in a stable life is, in his actual life, the source of his ethical core.

**Limits.** This clearing does not extend to threats against Marla or John. When the threat targets the small protected circle, he reverts to high-stress dysregulation and is at risk of catastrophic decisions. The Gargan/Venom event triggered the MI precisely because it was both — direct threat to his body and to the meaning of his life simultaneously.

---

## 6.7 Intimacy — The Rarest Footage

Surveillance of Jameson with the small circle (Marla, John, Robbie, Betty Brant in her long tenure, Ben Urich, and — eventually, awkwardly — Peter Parker) shows behaviors that almost never appear elsewhere.

**With Marla.** Volume halved. The cigar is set down when she enters the room. He stands when she sits — a 1940s-class courtesy he does not extend even to mayors. He calls her by her name, not by a diminutive; the formality is itself the tenderness. Physical contact is sparing but specific: hand to the small of her back when guiding her through a doorway, palm briefly cupping her elbow when she stands. He listens without interrupting for stretches that would be unimaginable in any other context. After her death, the absence of these micro-behaviors is itself the most visible mourning in the file — he does not perform grief; he stops performing courtesy, because the recipient is gone.

**With John.** Affection expressed through interrogation. *"Are you eating? Are you sleeping? What's the doctor saying?"* The questions are the love. He cannot say the sentence that the questions encode and has not, in the canonical record, ever said it cleanly. When John has been in actual danger, the behavior changes — he becomes the crisis-state Jameson of §6.6, calm and operational and willing to work with anyone, including Spider-Man, to retrieve his son. The willingness collapses again the moment the immediate danger is past.

**With Robbie.** A long and stable friendship encoded almost entirely in disagreement. They argue across the desk for hours; the argument is the relationship. Observable tells of the underlying bond: Jameson takes Robbie's calls at home, after hours, without irritation; he has, on multiple documented occasions, paid Robbie's legal or medical bills without acknowledgment; he refuses to discuss Robbie in the third person to anyone who is not also a confidant. He defended Robbie through the Tombstone frame-up at substantial cost to the Bugle and to himself.

**With Betty Brant.** Paternal in the displaced mode. He has known her since adolescence in story-time, has watched her trauma history accumulate, and treats her with a gentleness that surfaces in small things — he lowers his voice in her presence by reflex, he does not bark at her even on days when he barks at everyone, he asks after her by name in her absences.

**With Peter Parker.** Pre-unmasking, the relationship is the displaced caregiving described in §3 — opposition as love, payment as affection, criticism as engagement.
